</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Goldman_Sachs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs" data-section="43" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:30hudson.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/30hudson.jpg/220px-30hudson.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="291" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1117" data-file-height="1475"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 291px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/30hudson.jpg/220px-30hudson.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="291" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:30hudson.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Goldman Sachs Tower at <a href="/wiki/30_Hudson_Street" title="30 Hudson Street">30 Hudson Street</a> in Jersey City.</div></div></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Employee_satisfaction">Employee satisfaction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Goldman_Sachs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Employee satisfaction" data-section="44" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The company has been on <a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune Magazine</a>'s <a href="/wiki/100_Best_Companies_to_Work_For" title="100 Best Companies to Work For">100 Best Companies to Work For</a> list since the list was launched in 1998, with emphasis placed on its support for employee philanthropic efforts and high employee compensation levels.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Compensation">Compensation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Goldman_Sachs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Compensation" data-section="45" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In the first three months of 2016, the average total compensation per employee was $72,931 for the three months, 44% below the same period in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> The average total compensation per employee for the full year of 2006 was $622,000.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> The average compensation in the first three months of 2013 was $135,594.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> However, these numbers represent the <a href="/wiki/Arithmetic_mean" title="Arithmetic mean">arithmetic mean</a> of total compensation and are highly skewed upwards as several hundred of the top recipients command the majority of the bonus pools, leaving the median that most employees receive well below this number.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> In <i>Business Week'</i>s September 2008 release of the <i>Best Places to Launch a Career</i>, Goldman Sachs was ranked No. 4 out of 119 total companies on the list.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> It was ranked No. 62 on the list of best places to work by <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Fortune Magazine">Fortune Magazine</a></i> in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup></p><p>CEO Blankfein received a $67.9 million bonus in 2007, his first year. He chose to receive "some" cash unlike his predecessor, Paulson, who chose to take his bonus entirely in company stock.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> In 2011, the bank had nearly 11,000 more staffers than it did in 2005, but performances of workers drastically declined. In 2011, Goldman's 33,300 employees generated $28.8 billion in revenue and $2.5 billion in profit, but it represented a 25% decline in revenue per worker and a 71% decline in profit per worker compared with 2005. In 2011, the company reduced its workforce by 2,400 positions.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters2012March19LaCapraLaurenTara_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters2012March19LaCapraLaurenTara-252">[252]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Officers_and_directors">Officers and directors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Goldman_Sachs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Officers and directors" data-section="46" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Notable members currently on the <a href="/wiki/Board_of_directors" title="Board of directors">board of directors</a> of the company are
<a href="/wiki/M._Michele_Burns" title="M. Michele Burns">M. Michele Burns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_George_(professor_and_author)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bill George (professor and author)">William W. George</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_A._Johnson_(businessman)" class="mw-redirect" title="James A. Johnson (businessman)">James A. Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ellen_J._Kullman" title="Ellen J. Kullman">Ellen J. Kullman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lakshmi_Mittal" title="Lakshmi Mittal">Lakshmi Mittal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adebayo_Ogunlesi" title="Adebayo Ogunlesi">Adebayo Ogunlesi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Oppenheimer" title="Peter Oppenheimer">Peter Oppenheimer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Debora_Spar" title="Debora Spar">Debora Spar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Tucker_(business)" title="Mark Tucker (business)">Mark Tucker</a>, and <a href="/wiki/David_Viniar" title="David Viniar">David Viniar</a>. Directors receive annual compensation of $600,000.<sup id="cite_ref-proxy_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-proxy-253">[253]</a></sup></p><p>The company's officers are listed on its website as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup></p>

<td>
</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters_and_other_major_offices">Headquarters and other major offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Goldman_Sachs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Headquarters and other major offices" data-section="47" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1957, the company's headquarters was relocated to 20 <a href="/wiki/Broad_Street_(Manhattan)" title="Broad Street (Manhattan)">Broad Street</a>, New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-Cohan2012_15-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cohan2012-15">[15]</a></sup></p><p>Goldman Sachs's global headquarters is now at <a href="/wiki/200_West_Street" title="200 West Street">200 West Street</a>, New York City, and the company has major offices and regional headquarters in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">Salt Lake City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-reutersoverview_87-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reutersoverview-87">[87]</a></sup></p><p>The Bangalore office, inaugurated among much fanfare in 2019, was the third largest global office for Goldman Sachs.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional"><li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Goldman_Sachs_River_Court_Building_Fleet_Street_1977c.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Goldman_Sachs_River_Court_Building_Fleet_Street_1977c.jpg/69px-Goldman_Sachs_River_Court_Building_Fleet_Street_1977c.jpg" decoding="async" width="69" height="120" data-file-width="2666" data-file-height="4602"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 69px;height: 120px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Goldman_Sachs_River_Court_Building_Fleet_Street_1977c.jpg/69px-Goldman_Sachs_River_Court_Building_Fleet_Street_1977c.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="69" data-height="120"> </span></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Goldman Sachs River Court Building, <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Street" title="Fleet Street">Fleet Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Slc_222_south_main.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Slc_222_south_main.jpg/80px-Slc_222_south_main.jpg" decoding="async" width="80" height="120" data-file-width="3744" data-file-height="5616"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 80px;height: 120px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Slc_222_south_main.jpg/80px-Slc_222_south_main.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="80" data-height="120"> </span></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">Salt Lake City</a> office at <a href="/wiki/222_South_Main" class="mw-redirect" title="222 South Main">222 South Main</a>
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Goldman_Sachs_research_papers">Goldman Sachs research papers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Goldman_Sachs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Goldman Sachs research papers" data-section="48" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<p>The following are notable Goldman Sachs research papers:
</p>
<ul><li>Global Economics Paper No: 93 (South Africa Growth and Unemployment: A Ten-Year Outlook): Makes economic projections for <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> for the next 10 years. Published on May 13, 2003.</li>
<li>Global Economics Paper No: 99 (Dreaming With BRICs: The Path to 2050): Introduced the <a href="/wiki/BRIC" title="BRIC">BRIC</a> concept, which became highly popularized in the media and in economic research from this point on. Also made economic projections for 2050 for the <a href="/wiki/G7" class="mw-redirect" title="G7">G7</a> and South Africa as well. These were the first long-term economic projections covering the GDP of numerous countries. Published on October 1, 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup></li>
<li>Global Economics Paper No: 134 (How Solid are the BRICs): Introduced the <a href="/wiki/Jim_O%27Neill,_Baron_O%27Neill_of_Gatley#Next_Eleven" title="Jim O'Neill, Baron O'Neill of Gatley">Next Eleven</a> concept. Published on December 1, 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup></li>
<li>Global Economics Paper No: 173 (New EU Member States - A Fifth BRIC?): Makes 2050 economic projections for the new <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> member states as a whole. Published on September 26, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup></li>
<li>Global Economics Paper No: 188 (A United Korea; Reassessing North Korea Risks (Part I)): Makes 2050 economic projections for North Korea in the hypothetical event that North Korea makes large free-market reforms right now. Published on September 21, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Olympics and Economics 2012: Makes projections for the number of gold medals and told Olympic medals that each country wins at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="2012 Olympics">2012 Olympics</a> using economic data and previous Olympic data. Published in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup></li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Goldman_Sachs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="49" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_former_employees_of_Goldman_Sachs" title="List of former employees of Goldman Sachs">List of former employees of Goldman Sachs</a></li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Goldman_Sachs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: References" data-section="50" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">

<li id="cite_note-devils-p274-1-165"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-devils-p274-1_165-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Bethany McLean; Joe Nocera. <i>All the Devils Are Here: The Hidden History of the Financial Crisis</i>. p. 274. <q>The CDO had been constructed, Goldman executives later told the Senate Permanent Subcommittee, while the company was trying to remove triple-B assets from its books. Among those assets was a long position in the ABX index that Goldman had gotten 'stuck' with while putting together deals for hedge fund clients that wanted to go short. Unable to find counterparties to take the long position off its hands, Goldman used Hudson as a means by which it hedged its long position. ... None of which was clear from the Hudson prospectus. Instead, the disclosure merely said that the CDO's contents were 'assets sourced from the Street', making it sound as though Goldman randomly selected the securities, instead of specifically creating a hedge for its won book.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=All+the+Devils+Are+Here%3A+The+Hidden+History+of+the+Financial+Crisis&amp;rft.pages=274&amp;rft.au=Bethany+McLean&amp;rft.au=Joe+Nocera&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGoldman+Sachs" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>

<li id="cite_note-7pillars-168"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-7pillars_168-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-7pillars_168-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-7pillars_168-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Whalen, Philip; Tan Bhala, Kara. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://sevenpillarsinstitute.org/case-studies/goldman-sachs-and-the-abacus-deal">"Goldman Sachs and The ABACUS Deal"</a>. <a href="/wiki/Seven_Pillars_Institute" title="Seven Pillars Institute">Seven Pillars Institute</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Goldman+Sachs+and+The+ABACUS+Deal&amp;rft.pub=Seven+Pillars+Institute&amp;rft.aulast=Whalen&amp;rft.aufirst=Philip&amp;rft.au=Tan+Bhala%2C+Kara&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fsevenpillarsinstitute.org%2Fcase-studies%2Fgoldman-sachs-and-the-abacus-deal&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGoldman+Sachs" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>

<li id="cite_note-Reuters2010April16WilchinsDan-169"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Reuters2010April16WilchinsDan_169-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Reuters2010April16WilchinsDan_169-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Wilchins, Dan; Brettell, Karen (April 16, 2010). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.reuters.com/article/us-goldmansachs-abacus-factbox/factbox-how-goldmans-abacus-deal-worked-idUSTRE63F5CZ20100416">"Factbox: How Goldman's ABACUS deal worked"</a> (Business News). New York, N.Y., United States: Reuters. Thompson Reuters<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">February 9,</span> 2014</span>. <q><i>Hedge fund manager John Paulson tells Goldman Sachs in late 2006 he wants to bet against risky subprime mortgages using derivatives. The risky mortgage bonds that Paulson wanted to short were essentially subprime home loans that had been repackaged into bonds. The bonds were rated "BBB", meaning that as the home loans defaulted, these bonds would be among the first to feel the pain.</i></q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=Factbox%3A+How+Goldman%27s+ABACUS+deal+worked&amp;rft.issue=Business+News&amp;rft.date=2010-04-16&amp;rft.aulast=Wilchins&amp;rft.aufirst=Dan&amp;rft.au=Brettell%2C+Karen&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.reuters.com%2Farticle%2Fus-goldmansachs-abacus-factbox%2Ffactbox-how-goldmans-abacus-deal-worked-idUSTRE63F5CZ20100416&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGoldman+Sachs" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-170"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-170">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The $15 million has been described as "rent" for the Abacus name. <br><cite class="citation book">Bethany McLean; Joe Nocera. <i>All the Devils Are Here: The Hidden History of the Financial Crisis</i>. p. 279. <q>Paulson knocked on Goldman's door at a fortuitous moment. The firm had begun thinking about 'ABACUS-renal strategies' ... By that, he meant that Goldman would 'rent' - for a hefty fee - the Abacus brand to a hedge fund that wanted to make a massive short bet. ... Paulson paid Goldman $15 million to rent the Abacus name.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=All+the+Devils+Are+Here%3A+The+Hidden+History+of+the+Financial+Crisis&amp;rft.pages=279&amp;rft.au=Bethany+McLean&amp;rft.au=Joe+Nocera&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGoldman+Sachs" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Reuters2010April19SalmonFelix-171"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Reuters2010April19SalmonFelix_171-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Reuters2010April19SalmonFelix_171-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Salmon, Felix (April 19, 2010). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://blogs.reuters.com/felix-salmon/2010/04/19/goldmans-misleading-statement-on-aca/">"Goldman's misleading statement on ACA"</a> (Blogs). Reuters. Thompson Reuters<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 14,</span> 2010</span>. <q>when Goldman wrapped the super-senior tranche of the Abacus deal, it did so with ABN Amro, a too-big-to-fail bank, and not with ACA. ABN Amro then laid off that risk onto ACA, but was on the hook for all of it if ACA went bust. As, of course, it did.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=Goldman%27s+misleading+statement+on+ACA&amp;rft.issue=Blogs&amp;rft.date=2010-04-19&amp;rft.aulast=Salmon&amp;rft.aufirst=Felix&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fblogs.reuters.com%2Ffelix-salmon%2F2010%2F04%2F19%2Fgoldmans-misleading-statement-on-aca%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGoldman+Sachs" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>

<li id="cite_note-NewYorkTimes2010April22ThomasLandon-173"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-NewYorkTimes2010April22ThomasLandon_173-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Thomas, Landon (April 22, 2010). <span class="cs1-lock-limited" title="Free access subject to limited trial, subscription normally required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2010/04/23/business/23cdo.html">"A Routine Deal Became an $840 Million Mistake"</a></span>. <i>New York Times</i> (Business). [Royal Bank of Scotland] became involved in Abacus almost by accident. Bankers working in London for ABN Amro, a Dutch bank that was later acquired by R.B.S., agreed to stand behind a portfolio of American mortgage investments that were used in the deal. ABN Amro shouldered almost all of the risks for what, in retrospect, might seem like a small reward: that $7 million. <li id="cite_note-sanders-209"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-sanders_209-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-sanders_209-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://fuelfix.com/blog/2011/08/29/big-banks-bet-crude-oil-prices-would-fall-in-2008-run-up-leaked-data-show/">"Big Banks Bet Crude Oil Prices Would Fall in 2008 Run-Up, Leaked Data Show"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_L.P." title="Bloomberg L.P.">Bloomberg L.P.</a></i> <q>Just before crude oil hit its record high in mid-2008, 15 of the world's largest banks were betting that prices would fall, according to private trading data released by U.S. Senator Bernie Sanders. The net positions of the banks undermine arguments made by Sanders that speculative trades on Wall Street drove oil prices in 2008, said Craig Pirrong, director of the Global Energy Management Institute at the University of Houston. Retail gasoline reached a record $4.08 a gallon on July 7, 2008, and oil peaked at $147.27 a barrel on July 11 that year.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Bloomberg+L.P.&amp;rft.atitle=Big+Banks+Bet+Crude+Oil+Prices+Would+Fall+in+2008+Run-Up%2C+Leaked+Data+Show&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Ffuelfix.com%2Fblog%2F2011%2F08%2F29%2Fbig-banks-bet-crude-oil-prices-would-fall-in-2008-run-up-leaked-data-show%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGoldman+Sachs" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>
